     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_.26_Sciences">Arts &amp; Sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Arts &amp; Sciences">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Arts_and_Sciences_at_Washington_University_in_St._Louis" title="Arts and Sciences at Washington University in St. Louis">Arts and Sciences at Washington University in St. Louis</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Holmes_Lounge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Holmes_Lounge.jpg/220px-Holmes_Lounge.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Holmes_Lounge.jpg/330px-Holmes_Lounge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Holmes_Lounge.jpg/440px-Holmes_Lounge.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Holmes_Lounge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Holmes Lounge, the central reading room on campus, where students may eat and study
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>For the Fall 2011 semester Arts &amp; Sciences enrolled 942 out of 18,079 applicants (5.2%).</p> 
     <p>Arts &amp; Sciences at Washington University comprises three divisions: the College of Arts &amp; Sciences, the Graduate School of Arts &amp; Sciences, and University College in Arts &amp; Sciences. <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Schaal" title="Barbara Schaal" class="mw-redirect">Barbara Schaal</a> is Dean of the Faculty of Arts &amp; Sciences. <a href="/w/index.php?title=James_E._McLeod&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="James E. McLeod (page does not exist)">James E. McLeod</a> was the Vice Chancellor for Students and Dean of the College of Arts &amp; Sciences; according to a University news release he died at the University's <a href="/wiki/Barnes-Jewish_Hospital" title="Barnes-Jewish Hospital">Barnes-Jewish Hospital</a> on Tuesday, September 6, 2011 of <a href="/wiki/Renal_failure" title="Renal failure">renal failure</a> as a result of a two-year-long struggle with cancer. <a href="/wiki/Richard_J._Smith" title="Richard J. Smith">Richard J. Smith</a> is Dean of the Graduate School of Arts &amp; Sciences.</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The College of Arts &amp; Sciences is the central undergraduate unit of the University with 330 tenured and <a href="/wiki/Tenure" title="Tenure" class="mw-redirect">tenure</a>-track faculty along with over 100 research scientists, lecturers, <a href="/wiki/Artist_in_residence" title="Artist in residence" class="mw-redirect">artists in residence</a>, and visitors serving more than 3,700 undergraduates in 40 academic departments divided into divisions of Humanities, <a href="/wiki/Social_sciences" title="Social sciences" class="mw-redirect">Social Sciences</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Natural_science" title="Natural science">Natural Sciences</a> and Mathematics. The College of Arts &amp; Sciences has an average class size of 18 students, with over 80% having fewer than 24. Almost one-half of the undergraduate classes have fewer than 10 students. The student-faculty ratio is 7:1.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The Graduate School serves over 1,800 students pursuing Master's and PhD degrees.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>University College grants both graduate and undergraduate degrees, offering courses primarily in the evenings for adult and continuing education.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The College of Arts &amp; Sciences offers courses in over a dozen languages, including <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic" class="mw-redirect">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hebrew" title="Hebrew" class="mw-redirect">Hebrew</a>, Spanish, German, French, <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>, Chinese, Japanese, Korean, Russian, Greek, Italian, <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a>, Portuguese, and <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>. University College in Arts &amp; Sciences also offers course work in Swedish, <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">Vietnamese</a>, and Czech.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business">Business</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Business">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Olin_Business_School" title="Olin Business School">Olin Business School</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:WUSTLKnight.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/WUSTLKnight.jpg/220px-WUSTLKnight.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/WUSTLKnight.jpg/330px-WUSTLKnight.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/WUSTLKnight.jpg/440px-WUSTLKnight.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:WUSTLKnight.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Knight Executive Education Center is a part of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Olin_Business_School" title="Olin Business School">Olin Business School</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Founded as the School of Commerce and Finance in 1917, the <a href="/wiki/Olin_Business_School" title="Olin Business School">Olin Business School</a> was named after entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/John_M._Olin" title="John M. Olin">John M. Olin</a> in 1988. The school's academic programs include BSBA, MBA, Professional MBA (PMBA), Executive MBA (EMBA), MS in Finance, MS in Supply Chain Management, Master of Accounting, and Doctorate programs, as well as non-degree <a href="/wiki/Executive_Education" title="Executive Education" class="mw-redirect">executive education</a>. In 2002, an <a href="/wiki/Executive_MBA" title="Executive MBA" class="mw-redirect">Executive MBA</a> program was established in Shanghai, in cooperation with <a href="/wiki/Fudan_University" title="Fudan University">Fudan University</a>.</p> 
     <p>Olin has a network of more than 16,000 alumni worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> Over the last several years, the school’s endowment has increased to $213 <a href="/wiki/Million" title="Million">million</a> (2004) and annual gifts average $12 million per year.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Simon Hall was opened in 1986 after a donation from John E. Simon.</p> 
     <p>Undergraduate BSBA students take 40–60% of their courses within the business school and are able to formally declare majors in eight areas: accounting, entrepreneurship, finance, healthcare management, marketing, <a href="/wiki/Managerial_economics" title="Managerial economics">managerial economics</a> and strategy, organization and <a href="/wiki/Human_resources" title="Human resources">human resources</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Business" title="International Business" class="mw-redirect">international business</a>, and operations and <a href="/wiki/Supply_chain_management" title="Supply chain management">supply chain management</a>. Graduate students are able to pursue an MBA either full-time or part-time. Students may also take elective courses from other disciplines at Washington University, including law and many other fields. Mahendra R. Gupta is the Dean of the Olin Business School.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Design_.26_Visual_Arts">Design &amp; Visual Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Design &amp; Visual Arts">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Sam_Fox_School_of_Design_%26_Visual_Arts" title="Sam Fox School of Design &amp; Visual Arts">Sam Fox School of Design &amp; Visual Arts</a>
     </div> 
     <p>For the Fall 2011 semester Design &amp; Visual Arts enrolled 106 out of 1,422 applicants (7.5%).</p> 
     <p>Created in 2005 by merging the existing Colleges of Art and Architecture, the Sam Fox School of Design &amp; Visual Arts combines the strengths of these fields into a single collaborative unit offering both undergraduate and graduate programs. The School comprises:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>College of Architecture</li> 
      <li>Graduate School of Architecture &amp; Urban Design</li> 
      <li>College of Art</li> 
      <li>Graduate School of Art</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Mildred_Lane_Kemper_Art_Museum" title="Mildred Lane Kemper Art Museum">Mildred Lane Kemper Art Museum</a>, considered one of the most distinguished university art collections in the country<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Architecture offers BS and BA degrees as well as M. Arch and MUD. There is a combined six-year BS and M. Arch degree program as well as joint M. Arch programs with most of the other schools in the University. The Graduate School of Architecture and <a href="/wiki/Urban_design" title="Urban design">Urban Design</a> was ranked 5th in the nation by the journal <i>DesignIntelligence</i> in its 2008 edition of &quot;America's Best Architecture &amp; Design Schools.&quot;</p> 
     <p>Art offers the BFA and MFA in Art in the context of a full university environment. Students take courses in the College of Arts &amp; Sciences as well as courses in the <a href="/wiki/Art_school" title="Art school">College of Art</a> to provide a well rounded background. One third of students in the school pursue a combined study degree program, second major, and/or minors in other undergraduate divisions at Washington University<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranked the MFA program 13th in the nation in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In October 2006 the Mildred Lane Kemper Art Museum moved into new facilities designed by <a href="/wiki/Pritzker_Prize" title="Pritzker Prize" class="mw-redirect">Pritzker Prize</a>-winning architect, and former faculty member, <a href="/wiki/Fumihiko_Maki" title="Fumihiko Maki">Fumihiko Maki</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Carmon Colangelo is the Dean of the Sam Fox School of Design &amp; Visual Arts. Bruce Lindsey is Dean of the College of Architecture and the Graduate School of Architecture &amp; Urban Design. Franklin &quot;Buzz&quot; Spector is the Dean of the College and Graduate School of Art.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Engineering">Engineering</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Engineering">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_University_School_of_Engineering" title="Washington University School of Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Washington University School of Engineering</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:223975611_347a8f740b_b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/223975611_347a8f740b_b.jpg/170px-223975611_347a8f740b_b.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/223975611_347a8f740b_b.jpg/255px-223975611_347a8f740b_b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/223975611_347a8f740b_b.jpg/340px-223975611_347a8f740b_b.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:223975611_347a8f740b_b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Cupples Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>For the Fall 2011 semester Engineering enrolled 272 out of 5,162 applicants (5.3%).</p> 
     <p>The Washington University School of Engineering was ranked 48 in the 2012–2013 <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News</a></i> undergraduate engineering program ratings. The biomedical engineering graduate program was ranked 12th by <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News</a> in 2012–2013. Graduate programs are also offered through the School of Engineering and part-time programs through the Sever Institute of Continuing Studies. Ralph Quatrano is Dean of Engineering &amp; Applied Science.</p> 
     <p>Departments include:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Biomedical_Engineering" title="Biomedical Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Biomedical Engineering</a> - ranked 12 by <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Computer_Science_and_Engineering" title="Computer Science and Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Computer Science and Engineering</a> - ranked 38 by <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Electrical_Engineering" title="Electrical Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Electrical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Systems_Engineering" title="Systems Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Systems Engineering</a> - ranked 51 by <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News</a></li> 
      <li>Energy, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Engineering" title="Environmental Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Environmental</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Engineering" title="Chemical Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Chemical Engineering</a>- ranked 38 by <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News</a>. Will be housed in 2010 in the new Brauer Hall building, named after <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hunter_Engineering_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hunter Engineering Company (page does not exist)">Hunter Engineering Company</a> CEO and former Ambassador to Belgium <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_F._Brauer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stephen F. Brauer (page does not exist)">Stephen F. Brauer</a> and his wife Camilla</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Mechanical_Engineering" title="Mechanical Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Mechanical Engineering</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Materials_Science" title="Materials Science" class="mw-redirect">Materials Science</a> - ranked 44 by <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News</a></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law">Law</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Law">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_University_School_of_Law" title="Washington University School of Law">Washington University School of Law</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:WashUABhall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/WashUABhall.jpg/220px-WashUABhall.jpg" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/WashUABhall.jpg/330px-WashUABhall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/WashUABhall.jpg/440px-WashUABhall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:WashUABhall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Anheuser Busch Hall, home to the 
        <a href="/wiki/Washington_University_School_of_Law" title="Washington University School of Law">School of Law</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Washington University School of Law offers joint-degree programs with the Olin Business School, the Graduate School of Arts and Sciences, the School of Medicine, and the School of Social Work. It also offers an LLM in Intellectual Property and Technology Law, an LLM in Taxation, an LLM in US Law for Foreign Lawyers, a Master of Juridical Studies (MJS), and a Juris Scientiae Doctoris (JSD). The <a href="/wiki/Law_school" title="Law school">law school</a> offers 3 semesters of courses in the Spring, Summer, and Fall, and requires at least 85 hours of coursework for the JD.</p> 
     <p>In the 2013 <i>US News &amp; World Report</i> America's Best Graduate Schools, the law school is ranked 19th nationally, out of over 180 law schools.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> In particular, its <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://law.wustl.edu/clinics_programs/index.asp">Clinical Education Program</a> is currently ranked 4th in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> This year, the median score placed the average student in the 96th percentile of test takers.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> The law school offers a <a href="/wiki/Full_time" title="Full time" class="mw-redirect">full-time</a> day program, beginning in August, for the J.D. degree. The law school is located in a state-of-the-art building, <a href="/wiki/Anheuser-Busch" title="Anheuser-Busch">Anheuser-Busch</a> Hall (opened in 1997). The building combines traditional architecture, a five-story open-stacks library, an integration of indoor and outdoor spaces, and the latest wireless and other technologies. <i>National Jurist</i> ranked Washington University 4th among the &quot;25 Most Wired Law Schools.&quot;</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Kent_D._Syverud" title="Kent D. Syverud">Kent D. Syverud</a> is the Dean of the School of Law.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medicine">Medicine</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Medicine">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Washington University School of Medicine">Washington University School of Medicine</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Washington_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Washington University School of Medicine">Washington University School of Medicine</a> is highly regarded as one of the world's leading centers for medical research and training.<sup id="cite_ref-grad-schools.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grad-schools.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> The School ranks first in the nation in student selectivity.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> Among its many recent initiatives, <a href="/wiki/The_Genome_Center" title="The Genome Center" class="mw-redirect">The Genome Center</a> at Washington University (directed by <a href="/wiki/Richard_K._Wilson" title="Richard K. Wilson">Richard K. Wilson</a>) played a leadership role in the <a href="/wiki/Human_Genome_Project" title="Human Genome Project">Human Genome Project</a>, having contributed 25% of the finished sequence.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> The School pioneered bedside teaching and led in the transformation of empirical knowledge into scientific medicine. The <a href="/wiki/Washington_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Washington University School of Medicine">medical school</a> partners with <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Children%27s_Hospital" title="St. Louis Children's Hospital">St. Louis Children's Hospital</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barnes-Jewish_Hospital" title="Barnes-Jewish Hospital">Barnes-Jewish Hospital</a> (part of BJC HealthCare), where all physicians are members of the school's faculty.</p> 
     <p>Within the <a href="/wiki/Washington_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Washington University School of Medicine">medical school</a>, the Program in <a href="/wiki/Physical_therapy" title="Physical therapy">Physical Therapy</a> is also highly reputable. It is ranked 2nd in the nation for &quot;Best Physical Therapy Schools&quot; according to <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> The Program offers a <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Physical_Therapy" title="Doctor of Physical Therapy">Doctor of Physical Therapy</a> (DPT) at both the professional and post-professional levels. In its 60-year history, more than 1,500 students, most of whom are still actively involved in the physical therapy profession, have graduated from the Program<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.</p> 
     <p>The Program in Occupational Therapy is currently tied for 1st in the nation for &quot;Best Occupational Therapy Schools&quot; according to <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-grad-schools.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grad-schools.usnews.rankingsandreviews.com-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> The Program offers a Master of Science degree as well as the Occupational Therapy Doctorate (OTD) at the professional and post-professional levels. M. Carolyn Baum, PhD, serves as the program director and was the most recent president of the American Occupational Therapy Association (AOTA).</p> 
     <p>Dr. Larry J. Shapiro, MD, is the Dean of <a href="/wiki/Washington_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Washington University School of Medicine">Washington University School of Medicine</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_Work">Social Work</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Social Work">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/George_Warren_Brown_School_of_Social_Work" title="George Warren Brown School of Social Work">George Warren Brown School of Social Work</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The George Warren Brown School of Social Work (commonly called the Brown School or Brown) is currently ranked first among <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Social_Work" title="Master of Social Work">Master of Social Work</a> (MSW) programs in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> Brown also offers a PhD in Social Work in cooperation with the Graduate School of Arts &amp; Sciences and a <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Public_Health" title="Master of Public Health" class="mw-redirect">Master of Public Health</a>. The school was endowed by Bettie Bofinger Brown and named for her husband&nbsp;— George Warren Brown&nbsp;— a St. Louis philanthropist and co-founder of the <a href="/wiki/Brown_Shoe_Company" title="Brown Shoe Company" class="mw-redirect">Brown Shoe Company</a>. The school is housed within Brown and Goldfarb halls. It has a center for Native American research, as well as acclaimed scholars in <a href="/wiki/Social_security" title="Social security">social security</a>, health, individual development accounts, etc. The school's current dean is Edward F. Lawlor.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_Schools">Former Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Former Schools">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Founded as the Missouri Dental College in 1866, the <a href="/wiki/Washington_University_School_of_Dental_Medicine" title="Washington University School of Dental Medicine">Washington University School of Dental Medicine</a> was the first dental school west of the Mississippi River and the sixth dental school in the U.S. The school closed in 1991.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_library_system">Museums and library system</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Museums and library system">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_University_library_system" title="Washington University library system" class="mw-redirect">Washington University library system</a>
     </div> 
     <p>With 14 libraries, the Washington University library system is the largest in the state of Missouri, containing over 4.2 million volumes.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The main library, Olin Library, is centrally located on the Danforth Campus. Other libraries in the system include:</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Olin_Library_wide.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Olin_Library_wide.jpg/220px-Olin_Library_wide.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Olin_Library_wide.jpg/330px-Olin_Library_wide.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Olin_Library_wide.jpg/440px-Olin_Library_wide.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Olin_Library_wide.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Olin Library in the Fall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Washington_University_Libraries#Specialty_libraries" title="Washington University Libraries">Kranzberg Art &amp; Architecture Library</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Washington_University_Libraries#Specialty_libraries" title="Washington University Libraries">Business Library</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Washington_University_Libraries#Specialty_libraries" title="Washington University Libraries">Chemistry Library</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Washington_University_Libraries#Specialty_libraries" title="Washington University Libraries">East Asian Library</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Washington_University_Libraries#Specialty_libraries" title="Washington University Libraries">Law Library</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Washington_University_Libraries#Specialty_libraries" title="Washington University Libraries">Medical Library (Becker)</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Washington_University_Libraries#Specialty_libraries" title="Washington University Libraries">Music Library</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Washington_University_Libraries#Specialty_libraries" title="Washington University Libraries">Physics Library</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Washington_University_Libraries#Specialty_libraries" title="Washington University Libraries">Social Work Library</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Washington_University_Libraries#Specialty_libraries" title="Washington University Libraries">Special Collections &amp; Archives</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Washington_University_Libraries#Specialty_libraries" title="Washington University Libraries">West Campus Library</a></li> 
     </ul> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Law_reading_room.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Law_reading_room.jpg/220px-Law_reading_room.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Law_reading_room.jpg/330px-Law_reading_room.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Law_reading_room.jpg/440px-Law_reading_room.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Law_reading_room.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Reading room in Anheuser-Busch Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Mildred_Lane_Kemper_Art_Museum" title="Mildred Lane Kemper Art Museum">Mildred Lane Kemper Art Museum</a>, established in 1881, is one of the oldest teaching museums in the country and the first art museum established west of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a><sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. The collection includes works from 19th, 20th, and 21st century American and European artists, including <a href="/wiki/George_Caleb_Bingham" title="George Caleb Bingham">George Caleb Bingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cole" title="Thomas Cole">Thomas Cole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Pablo Picasso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Max_Ernst" title="Max Ernst">Max Ernst</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Calder" title="Alexander Calder">Alexander Calder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Pollock" title="Jackson Pollock">Jackson Pollock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Rauschenberg" title="Robert Rauschenberg">Robert Rauschenberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Kruger" title="Barbara Kruger">Barbara Kruger</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christian_Boltanski" title="Christian Boltanski">Christian Boltanski</a>. Also in the complex is the 3,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;ft (300&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) Newman Money Museum. In October 2006, the Kemper Art Museum moved from its previous location, Steinberg Hall, into a new facility designed by former faculty member <a href="/wiki/Fumihiko_Maki" title="Fumihiko Maki">Fumihiko Maki</a>. Interestingly, the new Kemper Art Museum is located directly across from Steinberg Hall, which was Maki's very first commission in 1959.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research.2C_Research_Centers_and_Institutes">Research, Research Centers and Institutes</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Research, Research Centers and Institutes">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Brown_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Brown_Hall.jpg/220px-Brown_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Brown_Hall.jpg/330px-Brown_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Brown_Hall.jpg/440px-Brown_Hall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Brown_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Brown Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Centers_and_institutes_of_Washington_University_in_St._Louis" title="Centers and institutes of Washington University in St. Louis">Centers and institutes of Washington University in St. Louis</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Virtually all faculty members at Washington University engage in academic research, offering opportunities for both undergraduate and graduate students across the University's 7 schools. Known for its interdisciplinarity and departmental collaboration, most research centers and institutes at Washington University are collaborative efforts between many areas on campus. More than 60% of undergraduates are involved in faculty research across all areas;<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> it is an institutional priority for undergraduates to be allowed to participate in advanced research, which is rather unique among leading private research universities.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the Center for Measuring University Performance, it is considered to be one of the top 10 private research universities in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> A dedicated Office of Undergraduate Research is located on the <a href="/wiki/Danforth_Campus" title="Danforth Campus">Danforth Campus</a> and serves as a resource to post research opportunities, advise students in finding appropriate positions matching their interests, publish undergraduate research journals, and award research grants to make it financially possible to perform research.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>During fiscal 2007, $537.5 million was received in total research support, including $444 million in federal obligations. The University has over 150 <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health</a> funded inventions, with many of them licensed to private companies. Governmental agencies and non-profit foundations such as the NIH, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">United States Department of Defense</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> provide the majority of research grant funding, with Washington University being one of the top recipients in NIH grants from year-to-year. Nearly 80% of NIH grants to institutions in the state of Missouri went to Washington University alone in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Washington University and its Medical School play a large part in the <a href="/wiki/Human_Genome_Project" title="Human Genome Project">Human Genome Project</a>, where it contributes approximately 25% of the finished sequence.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> The Genome Sequencing Center has decoded the genome of many animals, plants, and cellular organisms, including the platypus, chimpanzee, cat, and corn.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>NASA hosts its Planetary Data System Geosciences Node on the campus of Washington University. Professors, students, and researchers have been very involved with many unmanned missions to Mars. Professor Ray Arvidson has been co-investigator of the Phoenix Rover robotic arm and chair of the Mars Exploration Rover landing site group.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Washington University professor Joseph Lowenstein, with the assistance of several undergraduate students, has been involved in editing, annotating, making a digital archive of the first publication of poet <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Spencer" title="Edmund Spencer" class="mw-redirect">Edmund Spencer</a>'s collective works in 100 years. A large grant from the <a href="/wiki/National_Endowment_for_the_Humanities" title="National Endowment for the Humanities">National Endowment for the Humanities</a> has been given to support this ambitious project centralized at Washington University with support from other colleges in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_life">Campus life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Campus life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Campus_life_at_Washington_University_in_St._Louis" title="Campus life at Washington University in St. Louis">Campus life at Washington University in St. Louis</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_organizations">Student organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Student organizations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:WUWomansBuilding.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/WUWomansBuilding.JPG/220px-WUWomansBuilding.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/WUWomansBuilding.JPG/330px-WUWomansBuilding.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/WUWomansBuilding.JPG/440px-WUWomansBuilding.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:WUWomansBuilding.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Women's Building
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Washington University has over 300 undergraduate student organizations on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Most are funded by the <a href="/wiki/Washington_University_Student_Union" title="Washington University Student Union" class="mw-redirect">Washington University Student Union</a>, which has a $2 million plus annual budget that is completely student-controlled and is one of the largest student government budgets in the country. Known as SU for short, the Student Union sponsors large-scale campus programs including <a href="/wiki/Walk_in_lay_down" title="Walk in lay down" class="mw-redirect">WILD</a> (a semesterly concert in the quad) and free copies of the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times" class="mw-redirect">New York Times</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Post-Dispatch" title="St. Louis Post-Dispatch">St. Louis Post-Dispatch</a></i> through The Collegiate Readership Program; it also contributes to the Assembly Series, a weekly lecture series produced by the University, and funds the campus television station, WUTV, and the radio station, <a href="/wiki/KWUR" title="KWUR">KWUR</a>. KWUR was named best radio station in St. Louis of 2003 by the Riverfront Times despite the fact that its signal reaches only a few blocks beyond the boundaries of the campus.<sup id="cite_ref-radio_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-radio-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> There are 10 fraternities and 7 sororities. The Congress of the South 40 (CS40) is a Residential Life and Events Programming Board, which operates outside of the SU sphere. CS40's funding comes from the Housing Activities Fee of each student living on the South 40.</p> 
     <p>Many of these organizations and other campus life amenities are housed in the $43 million <a href="/wiki/Danforth_Campus#Student_Centers" title="Danforth Campus">Danforth University Center</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Danforth_Campus" title="Danforth Campus">Danforth Campus</a>, also dedicated in honor of the Danforth family.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> The building opened on August 11, 2008 and earned <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a> Gold certification for its environmentally friendly design.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Washington University has a large number of student-run musical groups on campus, including 12 official <a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">a cappella</a> groups. The Pikers, an all-male group, is the oldest such group on campus. The Greenleafs, an all-female group is the oldest (and only) female group on campus. The <a href="/wiki/Mosaic_Whispers" title="Mosaic Whispers">Mosaic Whispers</a>, founded in 1991, is the oldest co-ed group on campus. They have produced 9 albums and have appeared on a number of compilation albums, including Ben Folds' <a href="/wiki/Ben_Folds_Presents:_University_A_Cappella!" title="Ben Folds Presents: University A Cappella!">Ben Folds Presents: University A Cappella!</a> The Amateurs,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> who also appeared on this album, is another co-ed a cappella group on campus, founded in 1991. They have recorded seven albums and toured extensively. After Dark<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> is a co-ed <a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">a cappella</a> group founded in 2001. It has released three albums and has won several Contemporary A Capella Recording (CARA) awards. In 2008 the group performed on <a href="/wiki/MSNBC" title="MSNBC">MSNBC</a> during coverage of the vice presidential debate with specially written songs about <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Palin" title="Sarah Palin">Sarah Palin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> The Ghost Lights, founded in 2010, is the campus's newest and only Broadway, Movies, and Television soundtrack group. They have performed multiple philanthropic concerts in the greater St. Louis area and were honored in November 2010 with the opportunity to perform for Nobel Laureate Douglas North at his birthday celebration.</p> 
     <p>The campus newspaper is <a href="/wiki/Student_Life_(newspaper)" title="Student Life (newspaper)">Student Life</a>. The paper is published twice a week under the auspices of Washington University Student Media, Inc., an independent non-for-profit organization incorporated in 1999. The paper was first founded in 1878, making it one of the oldest student newspapers in the country.</p> 
     <p>The campus political/entertainment talk radio podcast is WURD, which streams for free on iTunes. Its listenership spans multiple continents and its host website has been visited by thousands of listeners.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_life">Greek life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Greek life">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Washington University has ten fraternities and eight sororities on campus.</p> 
     <p><b>Washington University Interfraternity Council</b></p>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residences">Residences</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Residences">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:South40.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/South40.jpg/220px-South40.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/South40.jpg/330px-South40.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/South40.jpg/440px-South40.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:South40.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The South 40
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Washington University is number one on the Princeton Review’s “Best College Dorms” list for 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Over 50% of undergraduate students live on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Most of the residence halls on campus are located on the <b>South 40</b>, named because of its adjacent location on the south side of the <a href="/wiki/Danforth_Campus" title="Danforth Campus">Danforth Campus</a> and its size of 40 acres (160,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>). It is the location of all the freshman dorms as well as several upperclassman dorms, which are set up in the traditional <a href="/wiki/Residential_college" title="Residential college">residential college</a> system. All of the dorms are co-ed. The South 40 is organized as a pedestrian-friendly environment wherein residences surround a central recreational lawn known as the Swamp. Wohl <a href="/wiki/Student_activity_center" title="Student activity center">Student Center</a>, the Habif Health and Wellness Center (Student Health Services), the Residential Life Office, <a href="/wiki/University_police" title="University police" class="mw-redirect">University Police</a> Headquarters, various student-owned businesses (e.g. the laundry service, Wash U Wash), and the baseball, softball, and intramural fields are also located on the South 40.</p> 
     <p>Another group of residences, known as the Village, is located in the northwest corner of <a href="/wiki/Danforth_Campus" title="Danforth Campus">Danforth Campus</a>. Only open to upperclassmen and January Scholars, the North Side consists of Millbrook Apartments, The Village, Village East on-campus apartments, and all fraternity houses except the Zeta Beta Tau house, which is off campus and located just northwest of the South 40. Sororities at Washington University do not have houses by their own accord. The Village is a group of residences where students who have similar interests or academic goals apply as small groups of 4 to 24, known as BLOCs, to live together in clustered suites along with non-BLOCs. Like the South 40, the residences around the Village also surround a recreational lawn.</p> 
     <p>In addition to South 40 and North Side residence halls, Washington University owns several apartment buildings within walking distance to Danforth Campus, which are open to upperclassmen.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_media">Student media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Student media">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Washington University supports four major student-run media outlets. The university's <a href="/wiki/Student_newspaper" title="Student newspaper">student newspaper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Student_Life_(newspaper)" title="Student Life (newspaper)"><i>Student Life</i></a>, is available for students. <a href="/wiki/KWUR" title="KWUR">KWUR</a> (90.3 FM) serves as the students' official radio station; the station also attracts an audience in the immediately surrounding community due to its eclectic and free-form musical programming. WUTV is the university's <a href="/wiki/Closed-circuit_television" title="Closed-circuit television">closed-circuit</a> <a href="/wiki/Television_channel" title="Television channel">television channel</a>. The university's main student-run political publication is the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.wupr.org">Washington University Political Review</a> (nicknamed &quot;WUPR&quot;), a self-described &quot;multipartisan&quot; monthly magazine. Washington University undergraduates publish two literary and art journals, The Eliot Review and Spires Intercollegiate Arts and Literary Magazine. A variety of other publications also serve the university community, ranging from in-house <a href="/wiki/Academic_journal" title="Academic journal">academic journals</a> to glossy alumni magazines to <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.wunderground.wustl.edu">WUnderground, campus' student-run satirical newspaper</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Washington_University_in_St._Louis_Bear_logo.png" class="image"><img alt="Washington University Bears logo" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/0/0c/Washington_University_in_St._Louis_Bear_logo.png" width="150" height="116" class="thumbimage" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Washington_University_in_St._Louis_Bear_logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Washington University Bears logo
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Washington_University_Bears" title="Washington University Bears">Washington University Bears</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Washington University's sports teams are called the Bears. They are members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> and participate in the <a href="/wiki/University_Athletic_Association" title="University Athletic Association">University Athletic Association</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Division_III_(NCAA)" title="Division III (NCAA)">Division III</a> level. The Bears have won 19 NCAA Division III Championships— one in women's <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">cross country</a> (2011), one in men's tennis (2008), two in men's basketball (2008, 2009), five in women's basketball (1998–2001, 2010),<sup id="cite_ref-bearsports.wustl.edu_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bearsports.wustl.edu-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> and ten in women's volleyball (1989, 1991–1996, 2003, 2007, 2009)<sup id="cite_ref-http_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-http-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup>&nbsp;– and 144 <a href="/wiki/University_Athletic_Association" title="University Athletic Association">UAA</a> titles in 15 different sports.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The Athletic Department is headed by John Schael who has served as <a href="/wiki/Athletic_director" title="Athletic director">director of athletics</a> since 1978. The 2000 <a href="/wiki/Division_III_(NCAA)" title="Division III (NCAA)">Division III</a> Central Region winner of the National Association of Collegiate Directors of Athletics/Continental Airlines Athletics Director of the Year award,<sup id="cite_ref-John_Schael_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-John_Schael-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> Schael has helped orchestrate the Bears athletics transformation into one of the top departments in Division III.<sup id="cite_ref-John_Schael_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-John_Schael-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Washington University also has an extensive club sports program, with teams ranging from men's volleyball<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> to women's Ultimate Frisbee. Funding for club sports comes from the Student Union budget, as each club is deemed a campus group.</p> 
     <p>Washington University is home of <a href="/wiki/Francis_Field_(St._Louis)" title="Francis Field (St. Louis)" class="mw-redirect">Francis Field</a>, site of the <a href="/wiki/1904_Summer_Olympics" title="1904 Summer Olympics">1904 Summer Olympics</a>. <a href="/wiki/Francis_Field_(St._Louis)" title="Francis Field (St. Louis)" class="mw-redirect">Francis Field</a> is also home of the Washington University football, soccer, and track and field teams.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:238038658_c62059dc1f_b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/238038658_c62059dc1f_b.jpg/220px-238038658_c62059dc1f_b.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/238038658_c62059dc1f_b.jpg/330px-238038658_c62059dc1f_b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/238038658_c62059dc1f_b.jpg/440px-238038658_c62059dc1f_b.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:238038658_c62059dc1f_b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Gates at Francis Field
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Walk_In_Lay_Down" title="Walk In Lay Down">WILD</a>&nbsp;– Walk In, Lay Down, the semesterly concert in the Quad which brings in popular acts such as <a href="/wiki/R.E.M." title="R.E.M.">R.E.M.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guster" title="Guster">Guster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lil%27_Jon" title="Lil' Jon" class="mw-redirect">Lil' Jon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ben_Folds" title="Ben Folds">Ben Folds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Busta_Rhymes" title="Busta Rhymes">Busta Rhymes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Live_(band)" title="Live (band)">Live</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Eyed_Peas" title="The Black Eyed Peas">The Black Eyed Peas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Passion_Pit" title="Passion Pit">Passion Pit</a>, and <a href="/wiki/K%27naan" title="K'naan">K'naan</a>. For the 2011 Fall W.I.L.D. <a href="/wiki/Mike_Posner" title="Mike Posner">Mike Posner</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_White_Panda&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The White Panda (page does not exist)">The White Panda</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=OCD:_Moosh_%26_Twist&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="OCD: Moosh &amp; Twist (page does not exist)">OCD: Moosh &amp; Twist</a> performed on the campus.</li> 
      <li>Bauhaus&nbsp;– Annual <a href="/wiki/Halloween_costume" title="Halloween costume">Halloween costume</a> party sponsored by the Architecture School Council, held in a giant tent in front of Givens Hall.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Thurtene_Carnival" title="Thurtene Carnival">Thurtene Carnival</a>&nbsp;– The oldest and largest student-run carnival in the nation, run by Thurtene Honorary.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>Vertigo&nbsp;– A dance party put on by the Engineering School Council (EnCouncil), featuring an innovative 8-foot (2.4&nbsp;m) by 16-foot (4.9&nbsp;m) computer-controlled modular LED <a href="/wiki/Illuminated_dance_floor" title="Illuminated dance floor">illuminated dance floor</a> built by students. The dance floor has since become a hit in St. Louis<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.</li> 
      <li>Cultural Shows&nbsp;– Each year Washington University student groups put on several multicultural shows, one of which sells out within hours of tickets going on sale (Diwali). Ashoka, the South Asian student association, puts on a performance for <a href="/wiki/Diwali" title="Diwali">Diwali</a>, the Indian festival of lights, that includes a skit and dances; Black Anthology is a student-run performance arts show celebrating <a href="/wiki/African_American_culture" title="African American culture" class="mw-redirect">black culture</a>; Lunar New Year Festival is a collaboration between the many East Asian organizations on campus culminating in a show to celebrate the holiday with a skit and dances from <a href="/wiki/Chinese_culture" title="Chinese culture">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_culture" title="Japanese culture" class="mw-redirect">Japanese</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Korean_culture" title="Korean culture" class="mw-redirect">Korean</a> cultures; celebrating African culture, Africa Week and the African Film Festival are annual events hosted by the African Students Association; the Association of Latin American Students showcases various forms of Latin and Spanish dances during their performance, Carnaval.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chancellors">Chancellors</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Chancellors">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chancellors_of_Washington_University_in_St._Louis" title="List of Chancellors of Washington University in St. Louis">List of Chancellors of Washington University in St. Louis</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Since its founding, Washington University has been led by 14 Chancellors, beginning with <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Gibson_Hoyt" title="Joseph Gibson Hoyt">Joseph Gibson Hoyt</a> in 1858. <a href="/wiki/Mark_Stephen_Wrighton" title="Mark Stephen Wrighton" class="mw-redirect">Mark Stephen Wrighton</a> serves as the current Chancellor of the University.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Washington_University_in_St._Louis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Washington_University_alumni" title="List of Washington University alumni">List of Washington University alumni</a>
     </div> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Washington University counts more than 114,000 living alumni, 26 <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholars" title="Rhodes Scholars" class="mw-redirect">Rhodes Scholars</a>, and 22 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_laureates" title="Nobel laureates" class="mw-redirect">Nobel laureates</a> affiliated with the university as faculty or students at a point in their lives.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Notable recent graduates of the college include: former Missouri Senator <a href="/wiki/Jim_Talent" title="Jim Talent">Jim Talent</a>, Nevada Senator <a href="/wiki/Chic_Hecht" title="Chic Hecht">Chic Hecht</a>, and former Nebraska Congressman <a href="/wiki/Hal_Daub" title="Hal Daub">Hal Daub</a>; <a href="/wiki/George_Zimmer" title="George Zimmer">George Zimmer</a>, founder of <a href="/wiki/Men%27s_Wearhouse" title="Men's Wearhouse">Men's Wearhouse</a>; <a href="/wiki/Avram_Glazer" title="Avram Glazer">Avram Glazer</a>, chairman of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United" title="Manchester United" class="mw-redirect">Manchester United</a>; Pulitzer Prize-winning journalists Ken Cooper and <a href="/wiki/Hank_Klibanoff" title="Hank Klibanoff">Hank Klibanoff</a>; <a href="/wiki/Jon_Feltheimer" title="Jon Feltheimer">Jon Feltheimer</a>, CEO of Lionsgate films; actors <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sarsgaard" title="Peter Sarsgaard">Peter Sarsgaard</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Boys_Don%27t_Cry_(film)" title="Boys Don't Cry (film)">Boys Don't Cry</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/An_Education" title="An Education">An Education</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Flightplan" title="Flightplan">Flight Plan</a></i>) and <a href="/wiki/Harold_Ramis" title="Harold Ramis">Harold Ramis</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Ghostbusters" title="Ghostbusters">Ghostbusters</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Caddyshack" title="Caddyshack">Caddyshack</a></i>); baseball player <a href="/wiki/Dal_Maxvill" title="Dal Maxvill">Dal Maxvill</a>; and science-show host <a href="/wiki/Deanne_Bell" title="Deanne Bell">Deanne Bell</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Design_Squad" title="Design Squad">Design Squad</a></i>).</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Earlier undergraduate alumni include <a href="/wiki/J._C._R._Licklider" title="J. C. R. Licklider">J. C. R. Licklider</a>, pioneer in artificial intelligence; <a href="/wiki/Charles_Nagel" title="Charles Nagel">Charles Nagel</a>, founder of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Chamber_of_Commerce" title="U.S. Chamber of Commerce" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Chamber of Commerce</a>; <a href="/wiki/Julian_Hill" title="Julian Hill" class="mw-redirect">Julian Hill</a>, co-inventor of nylon; <a href="/wiki/Clyde_Cowan" title="Clyde Cowan">Clyde Cowan</a>, co-discoverer of the neutrino; <a href="/wiki/James_R._Thompson" title="James R. Thompson">James R. Thompson</a>, Governor of Illinois; <a href="/wiki/David_R._Francis" title="David R. Francis">David R. Francis</a>, Governor of Missouri; <a href="/wiki/William_H._Webster" title="William H. Webster">William H. Webster</a>, former Director of the FBI; U.S. Ambassador to Belgium <a href="/wiki/Sam_Fox" title="Sam Fox">Sam Fox</a>; <a href="/wiki/Edward_Singleton_Holden" title="Edward Singleton Holden" class="mw-redirect">Edward Singleton Holden</a>, President of the University of California; <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Lamb_Eliot" title="Thomas Lamb Eliot">Thomas Lamb Eliot</a>, President of Reed College; and <a href="/wiki/Abram_L._Sachar" title="Abram L. Sachar">Abram L. Sachar</a>, founding President of Brandeis University. Graduates of the College of Architecture include George Hellmuth, <a href="/wiki/Gyo_Obata" title="Gyo Obata">Gyo Obata</a>, and George Kassabaum, founders of <a href="/wiki/Hellmuth,_Obata_and_Kassabaum" title="Hellmuth, Obata and Kassabaum">HOK</a>, the world's fourth-largest architectural firm.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The <a href="/wiki/Washington_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Washington University School of Medicine">School of Medicine</a> graduated Nobel laureates <a href="/wiki/Earl_Sutherland" title="Earl Sutherland" class="mw-redirect">Earl Sutherland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Krebs" title="Edwin Krebs" class="mw-redirect">Edwin Krebs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Nathans" title="Daniel Nathans">Daniel Nathans</a>. Businessman and adventurer <a href="/wiki/Steve_Fossett" title="Steve Fossett">Steve Fossett</a> earned his MBA from the business school. Doctoral alumni include the former Presidents of Johns Hopkins, Clemson, Wake Forest, Morehouse, Mount Union, Yonsei, and Hong Kong University of Science and Technology. An alumnus of the Graduate School of Architecture, <a href="/wiki/C._P._Wang" title="C. P. Wang">C. P. Wang</a> (M.Arch 1973), designed <a href="/wiki/Taipei_101" title="Taipei 101">Taipei 101</a>, the world's second-tallest building.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Famous students who dropped out: <a href="/wiki/Charles_Eames" title="Charles Eames" class="mw-redirect">Charles Eames</a> (who was expelled for defending modernist architecture); <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_Williams" title="Tennessee Williams">Tennessee Williams</a> (who left in protest of not winning the poetry prize); <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_Rent-a-Car" title="Enterprise Rent-a-Car" class="mw-redirect">Enterprise Rent-a-Car</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Jack_C._Taylor" title="Jack C. Taylor">Jack C. Taylor</a> (who withdrew to fight in World War II); actor <a href="/wiki/Robert_Guillaume" title="Robert Guillaume">Robert Guillaume</a> (who withdrew to study opera); Pulitzer Prize winner <a href="/wiki/Bill_Dedman" title="Bill Dedman">Bill Dedman</a> (who left to become a newspaper reporter); and IQ-record holder <a href="/wiki/Marilyn_vos_Savant" title="Marilyn vos Savant">Marilyn vos Savant</a> (who says she withdrew because she was bored).</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Washington_University_faculty_and_staff" title="List of Washington University faculty and staff">List of Washington University faculty and staff</a> (past and present): economist and Nobel Memorial Prize winner <a href="/wiki/Douglass_North" title="Douglass North">Douglass North</a>; <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">husband and wife</a> biochemists and co-Nobel Prize winners <a href="/wiki/Carl_Ferdinand_Cori" title="Carl Ferdinand Cori">Carl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gerty_Cori" title="Gerty Cori">Gerty Cori</a>; physicist and Nobel Prize winner <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Holly_Compton" title="Arthur Holly Compton" class="mw-redirect">Arthur Holly Compton</a>; novelists <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Elkin" title="Stanley Elkin">Stanley Elkin</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Gass" title="William Gass" class="mw-redirect">William Gass</a>; poets <a href="/wiki/Carl_Phillips" title="Carl Phillips">Carl Phillips</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_Jo_Bang" title="Mary Jo Bang">Mary Jo Bang</a>; architect <a href="/wiki/Fumihiko_Maki" title="Fumihiko Maki">Fumihiko Maki</a>; neurologist and Nobel Prize winner <a href="/wiki/Rita_Levi-Montalcini" title="Rita Levi-Montalcini">Rita Levi-Montalcini</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sexology" title="Sexology">sex researchers</a> <a href="/wiki/Masters_and_Johnson" title="Masters and Johnson">William Masters and Virginia Johnson</a>; <a href="/wiki/United_States_Poet_Laureate" title="United States Poet Laureate">Poets Laureate</a> <a href="/wiki/Howard_Nemerov" title="Howard Nemerov">Howard Nemerov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mona_Van_Duyn" title="Mona Van Duyn">Mona Van Duyn</a>; sociologist and &quot;outlaw <a href="/wiki/Marxist" title="Marxist" class="mw-redirect">Marxist</a>&quot; <a href="/wiki/Alvin_Ward_Gouldner" title="Alvin Ward Gouldner">Alvin Ward Gouldner</a>; attorney, former Counsel to Vice-President <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a> and former Tennessee Attorney General <a href="/wiki/Charles_Burson" title="Charles Burson">Charles Burson</a>; writer and culture critic <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Early" title="Gerald Early">Gerald Early</a>; Economist, and former Chair of President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>'s Council of Economic Advisors, <a href="/wiki/Murray_Weidenbaum" title="Murray Weidenbaum">Murray Weidenbaum</a>; chemist <a href="/wiki/Joseph_W._Kennedy" title="Joseph W. Kennedy">Joseph W. Kennedy</a>, co-discoverer of the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_element" title="Chemical element">element</a> <a href="/wiki/Plutonium" title="Plutonium">plutonium</a>; computer scientist <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_S._Turner" title="Jonathan S. Turner">Jonathan S. Turner</a>, internationally renowned expert in <a href="/wiki/Computer_networking" title="Computer networking" class="mw-redirect">computer networking</a>; computer scientist <a href="/wiki/Raj_Jain" title="Raj Jain">Raj Jain</a>, pioneer in the field of <a href="/wiki/Network_congestion" title="Network congestion">network congestion</a>; and Law Professor <a href="/wiki/Troy_A._Paredes" title="Troy A. Paredes">Troy A. Paredes</a>, currently on leave as a commissioner of the SEC.</li> 
     </ul>
